- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid, 4-sulfanylbenzoic acid) show mixed results, but the presence of a sulfanyl group in a short chain tends to result in a high yield. This may be due to the thiol group acting as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CX3H]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` may not accurately capture the requirement of both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain. Consider using a pattern that ensures the presence of both functional groups in a linear sequence, such as `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']`.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 2, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` might be too broad and could match any aromatic carboxylic acid. Ensure that the phenyl group is directly attached to the carboxylic acid by using a more specific pattern like `['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]']`.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 3's SMARTS pattern `['[n][c]']` is too general and may match any pyridine-like structure. Use a more specific pattern such as `['c1ccncc1']` to ensure it matches a pyridine ring.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 4, the SMARTS pattern `['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` should ensure the sulfanyl group is in a short chain. Consider using a pattern like `['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` to ensure the correct structure.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5's SMARTS pattern `['c1oc2ccccc2c1C(=O)[OX2H1]']` is specific to benzofuran but may not match all benzofuran derivatives. Consider using a more flexible pattern like `['c1oc2ccccc2c1']`.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS pattern `['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12']` is specific to indole but may not match all indole derivatives. Consider using a more flexible pattern like `['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12']`.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7's SMARTS pattern `['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` may not accurately capture the proximity requirement. Consider using a pattern that ensures the hydroxyl group is adjacent to the carboxylic acid, such as `['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']`.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern `['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]']` should ensure multiple ether linkages. Consider using a pattern like `['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]']` to ensure the correct structure.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9's SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[CX3H]']` may not accurately capture the formyl group attached to an aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern like `['c1ccccc1C=O']`.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4](F)(F)F']` is correct for trifluoromethyl groups, but ensure it is applied correctly in the context of the molecule.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11's SMARTS pattern `['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` may not accurately capture the methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern like `['c1cc(OC)ccc1']`.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: For Rule 12, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` may not accurately capture the requirement of a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern like `['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]']`.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` may not accurately capture long aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern like `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` to ensure the correct structure.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['c1ccccc1C=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1cc(OC)ccc1'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['c1ccccc1C=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1cc(OC)ccc1'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Based on the current metrics, we can make the following observations and comments regarding the performance of the current rules:

1. **Train Support**: The current train support is 0.0549, which is lower than the previous train support values of 0.1667 and 0.1845. This indicates that the current rules apply to a smaller portion of the training data compared to the previous rules. While this might suggest more specific rules, it could also mean that the rules are too narrow and not capturing enough relevant cases.

2. **Train Confidence**: The current train confidence is 0.6551, which is an improvement over the previous train confidence values of 0.6352 and 0.5396. This suggests that when the rule conditions are met, the likelihood of the rule prediction being true is higher, indicating more reliable rules.

3. **Train Lift**: The current train lift is 1.3120, which is significantly higher than the previous train lift values of 1.2048 and 1.0559. A lift greater than 1 indicates that the rule is providing useful information beyond the baseline probability of the prediction. The current lift suggests that the rules are more effective in identifying cases where the prediction is true compared to the previous iteration.

4. **Train Leverage**: The current train leverage is 0.0106, which is positive and an improvement over the previous negative leverage values. Positive leverage indicates that the rule is capturing more cases than would be expected by chance, suggesting a stronger association between the rule conditions and the prediction.

**Analysis and Recommendations for Improvement:**

- **Focus on Increasing Support**: While the current rules have improved confidence and lift, the support is relatively low. Consider revising the rules to cover a broader range of cases without sacrificing too much specificity. This could involve generalizing some of the conditions or exploring additional features that might be relevant.

- **Maintain High Confidence and Lift**: The current rules have achieved a good balance of confidence and lift, indicating that they are effective in making accurate predictions. Any changes to increase support should aim to maintain or further improve these metrics.

- **Evaluate Rule Specificity**: Given the low support, it might be beneficial to evaluate whether some rules are too specific or if there are overlapping conditions that could be combined to increase coverage.

- **Iterate on Rule Conditions**: Experiment with modifying or adding new conditions to the rules to see if they can capture more relevant cases while maintaining high confidence and lift.

Overall, the current rules show promising improvements in confidence and lift, suggesting they are more effective in making accurate predictions. However, efforts should be made to increase the support to ensure the rules are applicable to a larger portion of the data.

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current validation accuracy of 0.4286 is significantly lower than the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules are not effective enough in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The drastic drop in validation accuracy indicates potential underfitting. The model may not be capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively, possibly due to overly simplistic or incorrect rules.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 3 consistently shows a negative SHAP value, indicating it might be contributing to underestimation. Conversely, Rule 10 often shows a positive SHAP value, suggesting it might be overestimating the loading in some cases.
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 3 and Rule 10 again appear frequently, indicating potential issues with these rules.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest a low probability of improvement with the existing rules. The significant drop in accuracy compared to previous iterations indicates that the current set of rules may not be capturing the necessary features or interactions.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - The SHAP analysis highlights that Rule 3 and Rule 10 are frequently involved in incorrect predictions. This suggests that these rules may need refinement or reevaluation to better align with the experimental data.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - Rule 10, which often shows a positive SHAP value for high loading predictions, should be reviewed. Consider whether the presence of a trifluoromethyl group truly hinders the reaction process as expected, or if there are exceptions that need to be accounted for.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - Rule 3, which frequently shows a negative SHAP value, should be reassessed. The assumption that a pyridine ring always enhances yield may not hold in all cases. Investigate if there are specific conditions or additional structural features that influence this rule's effectiveness.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address underfitting, consider introducing additional rules or modifying existing ones to capture more complex interactions. This could involve incorporating more nuanced structural features or considering the influence of other functional groups.

4. **Iterative Refinement Using SHAP Insights:**
   - Use the insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. For example, if certain functional groups consistently lead to incorrect predictions, explore whether additional contextual information (e.g., neighboring groups or steric effects) can be integrated into the rules.

5. **Evaluate Rule Effectiveness:**
   - Continuously evaluate the effectiveness of refined rules by monitoring changes in validation accuracy and SHAP values. This iterative process will help identify which modifications lead to improved predictions and which require further adjustment.

By focusing on these areas, the rules can be refined to better capture the complexities of the data, potentially leading to improved accuracy and more reliable predictions.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CH]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)O'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['c1ccccc1C=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1cc(OC)ccc1'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)O'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['c1cc(O)ccc1'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

**Comments and Suggestions for Improvement:**

- **Balancing Specificity and Generality**: While the increase in confidence and lift is positive, the slight decrease in support suggests that the rules may be becoming too specific. It might be beneficial to review the rules to ensure they are not overly restrictive, which could limit their applicability.

- **Iterative Refinement**: Continue the iterative process of refining the rules, using the current metrics as a guide. Aim to maintain or improve confidence and lift while also seeking to increase support, ensuring the rules remain broadly applicable.

- **Validation with Test Data**: While the current analysis focuses on training metrics, it is important to validate the rules with test data to ensure they generalize well. Monitoring test confidence and lift will provide additional insights into the rules' effectiveness.

Overall, the current iteration shows positive trends in confidence and lift, indicating progress in rule development. However, attention should be given to maintaining a balance between specificity and generality to ensure the rules remain applicable to a wide range of scenarios.

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some improvement in validation accuracy from 0.4286 to 0.5714. This suggests that the rules are becoming more effective, but there is still room for improvement as the accuracy is not yet close to the previous reference accuracies (0.76).

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy indicates that the model is learning better from the data, suggesting a reduction in underfitting. However, the test accuracy is not provided for the current iteration, making it difficult to fully assess overfitting. It would be beneficial to compare the validation and test accuracies to ensure the model generalizes well.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 9 and Rule 15) may be contributing to overestimation. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 3 and Rule 10) may be contributing to underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvements Interpretation:**
   - The improvement in validation accuracy suggests that the current rules are moving in the right direction. However, the accuracy is still below the reference, indicating that further refinement is needed to reach optimal performance.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that may be contributing to prediction errors. For instance, Rule 9 and Rule 15 often have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, suggesting these rules might be too lenient or broad. Rule 3 and Rule 10, with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, might be too restrictive or not capturing relevant features.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - **Rule 9**: Consider narrowing the conditions under which a formyl group leads to high loading. The electron-withdrawing nature might not always reduce yield, especially if other stabilizing groups are present.
   - **Rule 15**: Re-evaluate the impact of the acetamido group. It may not always introduce steric hindrance, especially in shorter chains or when other stabilizing interactions are present.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - **Rule 3**: The pyridine ring's coordination with metal centers might be more context-dependent. Consider additional structural features that enhance this interaction.
   - **Rule 10**: The trifluoromethyl group's impact might be mitigated by other electron-donating groups. Explore combinations that could lead to higher yields.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce cross-validation with a larger number of folds to ensure the model is not overfitting to specific subsets of data.
   - Consider incorporating additional features or interactions that might not be captured by the current rules.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine rules. For example, test the impact of modifying Rule 9 and Rule 15 on a subset of data to observe changes in SHAP values and accuracy.
   - Continuously evaluate the model's performance on unseen data to ensure improvements are not just due to overfitting to the training set.

By focusing on these areas, the rules can be refined to better capture the underlying chemistry and improve the model's predictive accuracy.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Advice 6**: Regularly review and update the rules as new data becomes available. This will ensure that the rules remain relevant and accurate over time.

**End of Advice**
---------------------------------------------------------------
Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CX3H]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- ** Suggestion 13 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` should be revised to ensure the presence of a long aliphatic chain. Consider using a pattern like `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']`.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: For Rule 14, the SMARTS pattern `['c1cc(O)ccc1']` should be revised to ensure the presence of a hydroxyphenyl group. Consider using a pattern like `['c1cc(O)ccc1']`.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: For Rule 15, the SMARTS pattern `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]']` should be revised to ensure the presence of an acetamido group in a linear chain. Consider using a pattern like `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]']`.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)[CX3H]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1cc(OC)ccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['c1cc(O)ccc1'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to have limited effectiveness, as indicated by the fluctuating validation accuracies. The initial validation accuracy was 0.4286, which improved to 0.5714, but then slightly decreased to 0.5143. This suggests that while some improvements were made, the rules are not consistently effective across different datasets.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting:**
   - The significant drop in accuracy from previous iterations (0.76) to the current iteration (0.5143) suggests potential overfitting to the training data. The model may not be generalizing well to unseen data, as indicated by the lower validation accuracy.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 9 and Rule 15) may be problematic. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 3 and Rule 12) may need adjustment.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement in the current rules. The iterative process has not yet reached a local minimum, as indicated by the fluctuating accuracies. Further refinement of the rules is necessary to achieve more consistent and higher accuracy.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - The SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules, such as Rule 3 and Rule 12, consistently have high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings. This suggests that these rules may be too restrictive or not capturing important features that contribute to high loading. Conversely, rules like Rule 9 and Rule 15, which have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, may be too lenient or capturing irrelevant features.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - Rules such as Rule 9 and Rule 15, which contribute to overestimated loadings, should be refined. Consider narrowing the conditions under which these rules apply or introducing additional criteria to better capture the nuances of high loading.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - Rules like Rule 3 and Rule 12, which contribute to underestimated loadings, should be adjusted. This could involve broadening the conditions or incorporating additional features that may influence loading.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address overfitting, consider simplifying the rules or reducing the number of rules to focus on the most impactful features. Additionally, incorporating regularization techniques or cross-validation strategies could help improve generalization.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values (positive or negative) and evaluate their impact on the model's performance. This iterative process should aim to balance the trade-off between model complexity and generalization.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider incorporating additional features or modifying existing ones to better capture the underlying chemistry of the modifiers and their interaction with the catalyst. This could involve exploring new chemical descriptors or leveraging domain knowledge to inform rule development.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 12 **: For Rule 12, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` may not fully capture the adjacency requirement. Consider using a pattern that specifies adjacency, such as `['c1ccccc1C(=O)O']`.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` for long aliphatic chains may not be specific enough. Consider using a pattern that specifies a minimum chain length, such as `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']`.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: For Rule 14, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][OX2H]']` for hydroxyphenyl groups may need refinement to ensure the hydroxy group is directly attached, such as `['c1cc(O)ccc1']`.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15's SMARTS pattern `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]']` for acetamido groups in a linear chain may need refinement to ensure the acetamido group is in a linear chain, such as `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]', '[CX3](=O)[NX3]']`.

** End of Suggestions **
---------------------------------------------------------------
Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[NX3]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)O'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['c1ccncc1'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[SX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2ccccc12'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1cc(OC)ccc1'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)O'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['c1cc(O)ccc1'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]', '[CX3](=O)[NX3]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid, pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid, 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxyl group may interfere with the reaction or catalyst interaction.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[n][c][c][c][c][c]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['[c]1[c][c][c]2[c][c][c][c][c]2[c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['[nH]1[c][c][c]2[c][c][c][c][c]2[c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CX3H]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Matrix Checker Message:
** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` may not accurately capture the requirement of both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain. Consider using a pattern that ensures the presence of both functional groups in a linear sequence, such as `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[NX3]']`.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern `['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[n][c][c][c][c][c]']` should be revised to ensure it captures the pyridine ring structure accurately. Consider using a pattern like `['[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1']` to specifically match the pyridine ring.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 7's SMARTS pattern `['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` does not account for the proximity of the hydroxyl group to the carboxylic acid. Consider using a pattern that specifies the hydroxyl group is adjacent to the carboxylic acid, such as `['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]']`.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern `['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` should be revised to ensure it captures multiple ether linkages. Consider using a pattern like `['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]']` to match multiple ether linkages more effectively.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` is too generic and may overlap with Rule 2. Consider specifying the adjacency of the aromatic ring to the carboxylic acid more clearly, such as `['[c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']`.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` should be revised to ensure it captures long aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern like `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` to ensure the chain is sufficiently long.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Ensure that the SMARTS patterns are tested against a diverse set of SMILES to verify their accuracy in capturing the intended chemical structures. This can help identify any mismatches or oversights in the current patterns.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[NX3]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n]1[c][c][c][c][c]1'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['[c]1[c][c][c]2[c][c][c][c][c]2[c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['[nH]1[c][c][c]2[c][c][c][c][c]2[c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CX3H]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
