Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. However, if the pyridine ring is part of a larger, sterically hindered structure (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), the yield may be low.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some improvement in validation accuracy, reaching 0.6 in the latest iteration. This is a positive trend compared to the initial accuracy of 0.42857142857142855. However, the improvement is not substantial enough to suggest that the rules are highly effective. The accuracy is still below the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76 for validation and 0.75 for test sets.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The iterative process seems to be addressing some overfitting issues, as indicated by the gradual improvement in validation accuracy. However, the model might still be underfitting, given that the accuracy has not reached the levels of the reference metrics. The rules may not be capturing all the necessary features or interactions to accurately predict the loading of modifiers.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 15) might be overestimating the loading. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 3) might be underestimating the loading.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The gradual increase in validation accuracy suggests that there is potential for further improvement. However, the current rules may need significant refinement to achieve accuracies comparable to the reference metrics.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules, such as Rule 15, consistently contribute to high loading predictions. This suggests that these rules might be too general or not accounting for specific interactions that lead to lower experimental loadings. Similarly, rules like Rule 3, which have negative SHAP values for high loading, might need adjustment to better capture the conditions under which high loading occurs.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high positive SHAP values, such as Rule 15, should be refined to better differentiate between conditions that lead to high and low loadings. This could involve adding more specific conditions or interactions that are known to reduce loading.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values, such as Rule 3, should be adjusted to better capture the conditions that lead to high loading. This might involve incorporating additional features or interactions that are currently not considered.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential underfitting, consider expanding the feature set used to generate the rules. This could involve incorporating additional chemical properties or interactions that are relevant to the catalytic process.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. This could involve testing new rules or modifications in a controlled manner to evaluate their impact on accuracy and generalization.

5. **Evaluate Rule Effectiveness:**
   - Continuously evaluate the effectiveness of the rules by comparing the predicted and experimental loadings. Use this feedback to make data-driven adjustments to the rules.

By focusing on these areas, the rules can be refined to improve both the accuracy and generalization of the model, ultimately leading to better predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. However, if the pyridine ring is part of a larger, sterically hindered structure (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), the yield may be low.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. However, if the pyridine ring is part of a larger, sterically hindered structure (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), the yield may be low.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[n][c][c][c][c][c]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['[c]1[c][c][o][c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['[c]1[c][c][n][c]1'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CX3H]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H][c]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

            continue

        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. However, if the pyridine ring is part of a larger, sterically hindered structure (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), the yield may be low.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` may not accurately capture the presence of both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain. - ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 3's SMARTS pattern `['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[n][c][c][c][c][c]']` should be revised to account for steric hindrance. Consider adding a condition to check for additional bulky groups that might lower the yield.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 7's SMARTS pattern `['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` should be adjusted to differentiate between short and long aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern that specifies the length of the chain, such as `['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX4][CX4]']` for short chains.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 8's SMARTS pattern `['[OX2][CX3][OX2][CX3][OX2]']` may not fully capture the presence of multiple ether linkages. Consider using a more flexible pattern that allows for varying numbers of ether linkages, such as `['[OX2][CX3][OX2]', '[OX2][CX3][OX2]']`.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` should be revised to ensure it captures the steric hindrance or electronic effects of an adjacent aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern that specifies the proximity of the aromatic ring, such as `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][c]']`.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` may not accurately capture long aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern that allows for varying chain lengths, such as `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]', '[CX4][CX4]']`.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 15's SMARTS pattern `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]']` should be revised to ensure it captures the acetamido group in a linear chain. Consider using a pattern that specifies the linearity of the chain, such as `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]', '[CX4][CX4]']`.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3][NX3]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[n][c][c][c][c][c]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group in a short chain
        ['[c]1[c][c][o][c]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['[c]1[c][c][n][c]1'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3][OX2]', '[OX2][CX3][OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CX3H]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][c]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid group and adjacent aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]', '[CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H][c]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX4]', '[CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 15: Acetamido group in a linear chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 11]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown improvement in validation accuracy from 0.4286 to 0.6571. This suggests that the rules are becoming more effective in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts. However, there is still room for improvement as the accuracy is not yet optimal.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The initial low validation accuracy of 0.4286 suggests potential underfitting, where the model was not capturing the complexity of the data. As the rules were refined, the accuracy improved, indicating better fitting to the data. However, the consistent improvement without significant fluctuation suggests that overfitting is not a major concern at this stage.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 15) may be overestimating the loading. Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 10) may be underestimating the loading.

4. **Accuracy Improvements Interpretation:**
   - The increase in validation accuracy suggests that the iterative refinement of rules is moving in the right direction. The model is likely capturing more relevant features and interactions, leading to better predictions.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules, such as Rule 15, consistently contribute to high loading predictions. This suggests that these rules may need refinement to avoid overestimation. Similarly, rules like Rule 10, which contribute to low loading predictions, may need adjustment to prevent underestimation.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high positive SHAP values, such as Rule 15, should be reviewed to ensure they are not overly broad or capturing irrelevant features. Consider narrowing the conditions or adding additional constraints to these rules.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values, such as Rule 10, should be adjusted to better capture the conditions that lead to high experimental loadings. This may involve relaxing certain constraints or incorporating additional features that are indicative of high loading.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential overfitting or underfitting, consider incorporating cross-validation techniques and expanding the feature set to include more diverse chemical properties. This can help the model generalize better to unseen data.

4. **Iterative Refinement Using SHAP Insights:**
   - Use SHAP analysis to identify which rules consistently contribute to incorrect predictions. Iteratively refine these rules by testing different conditions and evaluating their impact on model performance. This process should be guided by domain knowledge and experimental validation.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider adding new features that capture more complex interactions or chemical properties not currently covered by the existing rules. This could include features related to molecular geometry, electronic properties, or solvent effects.

By following these recommendations, the rules can be refined to improve the model's predictive accuracy and generalization, ultimately leading to more reliable predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

3. **Discrepancies and SHAP Analysis:**
   - Discrepancies between predicted and experimental values highlight areas for rule refinement. Rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 15) may overestimate loading, while those with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 10) may underestimate it.

4. **Rule Refinement Suggestions:**
   - **Rule 1**: Ensure both amino and carboxylic acid groups are in a linear sequence.
   - **Rule 3**: Use a pattern that specifically matches the pyridine ring structure.
   - **Rule 7**: Specify proximity of hydroxyl group to carboxylic acid.
   - **Rule 8**: Capture multiple ether linkages accurately.
   - **Rule 12**: Ensure adjacency of carboxylic acid group to aromatic ring.
   - **Rule 13**: Capture long aliphatic chains accurately.
   - **Rule 15**: Ensure acetamido group is in a linear chain.

5. **General Recommendations:**
   - Refine rules with high SHAP values contributing to incorrect predictions.
   - Adjust rules to better capture conditions leading to high experimental loadings.
   - Incorporate cross-validation and expand feature sets for better generalization.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. However, if the pyridine ring is part of a larger, sterically hindered structure (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), the yield may be low.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid
        ['[n][c]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1C(=O)O'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[CH]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Acetamido group
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern `['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]']` may not accurately capture long aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern that specifies a minimum chain length.

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. However, if the pyridine ring is part of a larger, sterically hindered structure (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), the yield may be low.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[NX3]'],  # Rule 1: Amino and carboxylic acid groups
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)O'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid
        ['c1ncccc1', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Pyridine ring
        ['[SX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 5: Benzofuran structure
        ['c1c[nH]c2c1cccc2'],  # Rule 6: Indole structure
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2H]'],  # Rule 7: Hydroxyl group near carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2]', '[OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2]'],  # Rule 8: Multiple ether linkages
        ['c1ccccc1C=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 10: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['c1cc(OC)ccc1'],  # Rule 11: Methoxy group on aromatic ring
        ['c1ccccc1C(=O)O'],  # Rule 12: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4][C;X4]'],  # Rule 13: Long aliphatic chain
        ['c1cc(O)ccc1'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxyphenyl group
        ['[NX3][CX3](=O)[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[CX3](=O)[NX3]']  # Rule 15: Acetamido group
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 10]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to be struggling with effectiveness, as indicated by the low validation accuracy of 0.4286. This is a significant drop from previous accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules may not be capturing the necessary features to accurately predict the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting:**
   - The significant drop in validation accuracy suggests potential underfitting. The model may not be capturing the complexity of the data, possibly due to overly simplistic rules or missing important features. The consistent low SHAP values for certain rules across multiple molecules indicate that these rules may not be contributing effectively to the model's predictions.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 3 consistently shows a negative SHAP value, indicating it might be underestimating the loading. Conversely, Rule 10 often shows a positive SHAP value, suggesting it might be overestimating the loading for molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement. The model's performance has not reached a local minimum, as indicated by the fluctuating accuracies across iterations. This suggests that further refinement of the rules could lead to better generalization and improved accuracy.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - The SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that are consistently contributing to incorrect predictions. For instance, Rule 3's negative SHAP values in cases of underestimated loadings suggest it might need refinement to better capture the features associated with high loading. Similarly, Rule 10's positive SHAP values in cases of overestimated loadings indicate it might be too aggressive in predicting high loading.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - For rules like Rule 10, which show high positive SHAP values in cases of overestimated loadings, consider revising the conditions under which these rules predict high loading. This could involve adding additional constraints or modifying the existing conditions to better align with the experimental data.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - Rules like Rule 3, which show high negative SHAP values in cases of underestimated loadings, may need to be expanded or adjusted to capture additional features that contribute to high loading. This could involve incorporating additional chemical properties or interactions that are currently not considered.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential underfitting, consider introducing new rules that capture additional chemical features or interactions. This could involve exploring new chemical groups or structural motifs that are not currently covered by the existing rules.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from the SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. This could involve testing new rule formulations on a subset of the data to evaluate their effectiveness before integrating them into the full model.

5. **Incorporate Additional Data:**
   - If possible, incorporate additional data or features that could help improve the model's predictions. This could involve using more detailed chemical descriptors or exploring machine learning techniques to identify new patterns in the data.

By focusing on these areas, the current rules can be refined to improve the model's accuracy and generalization, ultimately leading to more reliable predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both amino and carboxylic acid groups in a linear chain (e.g., 2-aminopentanedioic acid, 2-aminobutanedioic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This combination likely enhances interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group directly attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may provide stability or facilitate interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring may coordinate with the metal center, enhancing the catalytic activity. However, if the pyridine ring is part of a larger, sterically hindered structure (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), the yield may be low.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group in a short chain (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group may act as a ligand or stabilizing agent.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The fused aromatic structure may stabilize the catalyst or transition state.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with an indole structure (e.g., (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring may provide additional stabilization through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a hydroxyl group in proximity to a carboxylic acid (e.g., 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. However, if the hydroxyl group is on a longer aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid), the yield may be low due to steric hindrance.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with multiple ether linkages (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) generally result in a low yield. The presence of multiple ether groups might disrupt the interaction with the catalyst or substrate.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may reduce the reactivity of the modifier.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may hinder the reaction process.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a methoxy group attached to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy group may enhance the electron density of the aromatic ring, facilitating the reaction.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and an adjacent aromatic ring (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The steric hindrance or electronic effects may reduce the modifier's effectiveness.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a long aliphatic chain (e.g., octanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The long chain may introduce steric hindrance or reduce the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxyphenyl group (e.g., 3-(4-hydroxyphenyl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The hydroxy group may cause steric hindrance or disrupt the interaction with the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with an acetamido group in a linear chain (e.g., (2S)-6-acetamido-2-aminohexanoic acid) tend to result in a low yield. The acetamido group may introduce steric hindrance or alter the electronic environment unfavorably.
